Frequently Asked Questions


------------------------------

*   1
    
    Can I use a personal virtual address to establish residency? Does the state matter?
    
    No, you can’t establish residency with a virtual address. Most customers default to picking the same state in which they’ve established residency, but you don’t have to. Most people are able to establish residency with a friend or family member’s domicile, and then use their virtual address for pretty much everything else. Moreover, if you’re still exploring creative ways of establishing new residency without paying a lot for rent, you may want to pick a state with easier residency rules like South Dakota, Wyoming, Nevada, Texas, or Florida.
    
*   2
    
    How do I forward my mail from a friend or family member’s address?
    
    You can complete this USPS [Change of Address](https://moversguide.usps.com/mgo/disclaimer)
     service in just a few minutes, though it can take as long as 7-10 business days for the USPS to officially start forwarding your mail. There’s no reason to think it will affect your friend’s or family member’s personal mail delivery. The USPS has no trouble tracking and triaging mail by the name the mail is addressed to.
    
*   3
    
    How do I know when I have new mail?
    
    You can view your scanned mail online anytime through your secure dashboard. As a default, you’ll receive instant email notifications when new mail is available.
    
*   4
    
    Does this service include mail forwarding?
    
    Our Personal Virtual Address service is not a mail forwarding service. We only forward checks and debit or credit cards to a U.S. address you provide. All other mail is scanned in high-resolution color and securely uploaded to your account for easy online access. We do not accept packages or oversized deliveries and will return these to the sender.
    
*   5
    
    What happens after my mail is received?
    
    Once your mail is scanned and uploaded for you to view online, digital copies are securely stored for the entire length of your subscription. After 1-2 weeks, we securely shred the physical copies using enterprise-grade shredders and disposal processes. It’s all done with your privacy in mind—and it means less paper clutter for you.
    
*   6
    
    Why do I need to complete USPS Form 1583?
    
    To comply with federal postal regulations, all virtual address users must complete USPS [Form 1583](https://about.usps.com/forms/ps1583.pdf)
    . This form authorizes us to receive mail on your behalf and ensures your mail is handled legally and securely. Without this form, we cannot activate your mailbox. It is a required step for all customers using a Commercial Mail Receiving Agency (CMRA) like ours.
    
*   7
    
    What types of identity verification are accepted?
    
    To complete USPS Form 1583, you must submit two forms of identification. One must be a government-issued photo ID, such as a driver’s license or passport. The second ID needs to confirm your name and address, such as a lease agreement or mortgage, home or car insurance policy, voter card, or vehicle registration. All documents must be valid and unexpired. A driver’s license and passport can also be used together to satisfy the two-ID requirement. This process is required to activate your account and remain in compliance with USPS regulations.
    
*   8
    
    I’m a sole proprietor using a fictitious business name. How do I use your virtual address?
    
    You can use our Personal Virtual Address, but unfortunately, you must use your legal name, not your DBA. As a sole proprietor, you can receive mail related to your work as a self-employed contractor. However, the mail must still be addressed to you personally to qualify as personal mail.
    
*   9
    
    Is there a limit to how much mail I can receive?
    
    There is no limit to how much mail you can receive. Your account includes unlimited incoming mail and unlimited digital storage for scanned documents.

A business name is more than just a moniker; it's the cornerstone of your brand identity. A compelling name can captivate customers, leaving a lasting impression that drives loyalty and growth. In today's competitive marketplace, finding the perfect name can be daunting.

This guide explores the best business name generator of 2024, the art and science of crafting the perfect business name, tips for creating catchy names, and how AI tools can assist in the process.

Introduction to Business Name Generators
----------------------------------------

Your business name serves as your initial impression. It's the verbal handshake that introduces your company to the world. A strong name can evoke emotions, communicate your brand's essence, and make an indelible impression among your target audience. But how do you go from a blank slate to a name that truly stands out? Bizee's business name generator simplifies naming by providing compelling, unique, and relevant name suggestions. Below, we'll introduce you to the top features of our generator and offer tips on creating an effective business name.

Top Features of Our Business Name Generator
-------------------------------------------

Our advanced business name generator is designed to be your naming partner. It's more than just a tool; it's a creative catalyst. Our AI business name generator uses artificial intelligence to provide many unique and relevant name suggestions tailored to your specific business.

### Key Features That Set Us Apart

*   **Intuitive interface.** Using our tool is as effortless as brewing a cup of coffee. No tech expertise is required.
    
*   **AI-driven innovation.** Our AI goes beyond suggesting random words. It understands your industry, target audience, and brand values to provide highly relevant name options.
    
*   **Customization at your fingertips.** Fine-tune your search parameters with specific keywords, industry preferences, and desired name length to align perfectly with your vision.
    

With just a few clicks, you can quickly generate a list of potential names that align with your brand's identity. Save time and effort with our user-friendly platform designed to spark your imagination.

  ![Woman Is Paying For An Order With A Credit Card](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvYXJ0aWNsZXMvbWFpbi1jb250ZW50L3dvbWFuLWlzLXBheWluZy1mb3ItYW4tb3JkZXItd2l0aC1hLWNyZWRpdC1jYXJkLndlYnA/woman-is-paying-for-an-order-with-a-credit-card.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)

How to Generate a Business Name
-------------------------------

The journey to the perfect name combines creativity, strategy, and the right tools. Here's how to get started with our generator.

### Step 1: Unleash Your Inner Wordsmith

Here's how to tap into your creative spirit and generate a killer name for your venture:

*   **Brainstorm with passion**—jot down words, phrases, and concepts associated with your business.
    
*   **Combine and conquer**—experiment with different combinations, and don't be afraid to color outside the lines! .
    
*   **Puns, alliteration, and playfulness**—add a dash of personality with these linguistic tools.
    

Using your imagination and playing with words can go a long way in helping you come up with a creative and effective business name.

### Step 2: Harness the Power of AI

Our AI-driven name generator is your creative partner in this process. Simply input your keywords, and witness a cascade of creative possibilities. AI's ability to quickly analyze vast amounts of data and understand linguistic patterns can offer you a surprisingly fresh perspective. AI provides you with several advantages, including:

*   **Speed and efficiency**—generate countless name ideas in minutes.
    
*   **Unbiased suggestions**—overcome mental blocks and discover unexpected options.
    
*   **Continuous improvement**—our AI learns and adapts, refining its suggestions over time.
    

AI is a tool, not a substitute for human creativity. But you can use it as a springboard for your imagination.

### Step 3: Refine and Perfect: How to Come Up with a Catchy Business Name

Once you've generated a list of potential names, it's time to refine your options:

*   Availability check. Verify that your desired name is available as a domain, social media handle, and [trademark](https://www.uspto.gov/trademarks/basics/why-search-similar-trademarks)
    .
    
*   Feedback loop. Seek input from colleagues, friends, and potential customers. Present the name to them and gauge their reactions.
    
*   Simplicity is key. Keep in mind that a short, easy-to-remember name is often the most effective.
    
*   Relevance reigns. Ensure the name accurately reflects your business's mission and values.
    
*   Memorable magic. See if your friends and family think the name is easily memorable. A sticky name is a successful name.
    
*   Legal landscape. Consult an attorney to ensure your chosen name complies with trademark laws and regulations.
    

The perfect name balances creativity, practicality, and legal compliance. With careful consideration and a dash of intuition, you'll select a name that captures [your brand's essence](https://bizee.com/articles/marketing-branding/how-to-brand-your-business)
 and resonates with your target audience.

With just a few clicks, you can quickly generate a list of potential names that align with your brand's identity.

How to Come Up with a Catchy Business Name?
-------------------------------------------

A catchy name is more than one that just sounds good; it's a strategic choice. Here are some steps to help you create a unique and effective business name.

### Define Your Brand Identity

Clearly understand your business's mission, values, and target audience. For example, a high-end fashion boutique might target affluent young professionals seeking unique luxury items, while a casual dining restaurant could focus on families and young adults looking for affordable, tasty food.

### Brainstorm Keywords

List words and phrases that describe your business. For example, consider related words like plant-based, healthy, organic, and gourmet if you're operating a vegan restaurant.

### Use Our Name Generator

Input your keywords into our generator to receive name suggestions. Entering words like fitness, strong, and healthy could yield suggestions like StrongFit, HealthyHub, or ZenGym.

### Combine Creative Techniques

Use creative brainstorming and keyword merging to refine your options. For example, combining the words book and nook could lead to the generation of names like The Book Nook. Or, merging the words fast and food might inspire the name Speedy Eats.

### Narrow Down Your Options

Select the names that best represent your brand. For instance, a vegan bakery might choose Green Goodness, while a tech startup could opt for InnovateIQ.

### Testing and Validation

Check the availability of the names on domain registration sites and social media platforms. Ensure the name is not already in use or trademarked by another business. You might discover that The Book Nook is already taken as a domain name, prompting you to consider alternatives like Nook and Book or Book Nook Cafe.

### Legal Considerations to Protect Your Brand

Once you've found your dream name, it's vital to protect it. Conduct a thorough trademark search to avoid legal complications. [Registering your business name](https://bizee.com/business-formation/trademark-registration)
 with the appropriate government agencies is essential. A catchy business name should be memorable, relevant, and available. By following these steps and using our business name generator, you can create a name that perfectly captures your brand's essence.

# FCC Ham Radio Address Rules: Stay Compliant & Protect Your Privacy

[Learn more\
\
![](https://bizee.com/_next/image?url=%2F_next%2Fstatic%2Fmedia%2Fmobile.3db9b7ad.png&w=3840&q=75)](https://bizee.com/articles/business-formation/fcc-ham-radio-address-requirements#)

[](https://bizee.com/articles/business-formation/fcc-ham-radio-address-requirements#)
[Skip to content](https://bizee.com/articles/business-formation/fcc-ham-radio-address-requirements#main-webpage-content)

  

The Airwaves Are Listening
--------------------------

(And So Is the FCC)
-------------------

  

To outsiders, Ham radio might sound like a niche hobby—a relic of pre-internet communication. But for those in the know, it’s the heartbeat of connection. Whether it’s swapping call signs with operators across continents or coordinating local emergency efforts, Ham operators are a unique breed: passionate, resourceful, and fiercely dedicated to the power of radio.

  

But here’s the rub: the FCC enforces strict Ham Radio Address regulations, requiring all operators to register a valid mailing address. And they’re serious about it. When you register for a Ham radio license, your address isn’t just a footnote—it’s public record. It’s a regulation designed to keep the airwaves orderly, prevent misuse, and ensure operators can be contacted.

  

Logical? Sure. Convenient? Not so much.

  

The [address requirement](https://www.arrl.org/fcc-licensee-privacy#:~:text=If%2520you%2520do%2520not%2520want,%252DFri)
, while reasonable on paper, can feel like a privacy minefield in practice. Do you really want your home address searchable to anyone with an internet connection? For many operators, the answer is no. For others—especially those frequently on the move, part of clubs, or even international license holders—the question isn’t just about privacy; it’s about logistics.

  

Let’s unpack this balancing act: the fine line between compliance and comfort, and how the right address can save you from headaches, public exposure, and an unexpected FCC knock at your (virtual) door.

![Mail carrier delivering a newspaper to a house with blooming pink flowers and a green garden on a sunny day.](https://bizee.com/_next/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fs3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com%2Fbizee-website-assets%2Fmailman-carrying-the-mail-door-to-door.webp&w=1920&q=75)

### Why Does the FCC Care About Your Address?

  

The FCC’s address rule boils down to two things: access and accountability. If interference happens—say someone jams a frequency or causes chaos on the air—the FCC needs to find the operator behind the call sign. Fast.

  

Your registered address isn’t just a formality; it’s how the FCC knows where to send renewal notices, rule updates, or (gulp) violation warnings.

  

Mess up your address—by using one that’s invalid, outdated, or unreliable—and you risk missing critical communication. In extreme cases, that could mean fines, license suspension, or outright revocation. 

  

The FCC isn’t exactly in the habit of sending out old-school, stamped-and-sealed correspondence. Their preferred mode of communication? Email. Swift, efficient, and decidedly paperless. But don’t get too comfortable—while unlikely, a letter from the FCC could still find its way to your mailbox. Never say never.

### Will the FCC send mail to my house?

  

The FCC isn’t exactly in the habit of sending out old-school, stamped-and-sealed correspondence. Their preferred mode of communication? Email. Swift, efficient, and decidedly paperless. But don’t get too comfortable—while unlikely, a letter from the FCC could still find its way to your mailbox. Never say never.

Home Sweet Public Record?
-------------------------

  

So where do you list? The default answer—your home address—is the simplest, but simplicity comes at a cost. Since the [FCC’s database is public](https://www.fcc.gov/wireless/universal-licensing-system)
, your home address becomes accessible to, well… everyone.

  

The mailman? Sure. Your Ham radio buddy from Nebraska? Fine. But also: nosy neighbors, online lurkers, and that guy you argued with in the comments section of [r/AmateurRadio](https://www.reddit.com/r/amateurradio/)
.

  

### Are P.O. Boxes Allowed for Ham Radio Operators?

  

Yes, the Federal Communications Commission (FCC) allows P.O. Boxes for Ham radio operators, but they come with limitations. While a P.O. Box can serve as your official Ham Radio Address, it only accepts USPS mail, meaning you could miss critical FCC correspondence from private carriers like FedEx or UPS. Additionally, accessing your mail requires in-person visits during post office hours, which may not be convenient for everyone.

  

### Are Virtual Addresses Allowed for Ham Radio Operators?

  

Yes! Virtual addresses provide a legal and private alternative for your Ham radio address while ensuring FCC compliance. [](https://bizee.com/form/virtual-address-ham-radio)
A tidy solution to a messy problem. A virtual address gives you a real, physical mailing location that [satisfies FCC requirements](https://wireless2.fcc.gov/helpfiles/licensemanager/commonQuestions.html)
 without exposing your private life. It works for solo operators, digital nomads, and even Ham radio clubs juggling multiple members and shifting leadership.

  

Think of it as the middle ground: private, professional, and practical.

Why a Virtual Address is Ideal for Ham Radio Operators
------------------------------------------------------

  

*   **No More Trips to the Post Office** – Read your mail from anywhere, just like email.
*   **Scanned, Color Copies of Mail** – Get digital scans of QSL cards, bills, FCC notices, and more.
*   **Unlimited Mail Reception** – No size limits; receive as much mail as you need without worrying about overflow.
*   **FCC & USPS Compliant** – Meets all regulations while protecting your privacy.
*   **Real Street Address** – Works for FCC licensing, QSL exchanges, receiving bills, account statements, etc.
*   **Mail Forwarding Available** – Choose when and where to receive physical mail if needed.

So You’ve Got a License… Now Keep It Updated
--------------------------------------------

  

Here’s a pro tip: addresses aren’t forever. Life changes. You move. You upgrade your setup. You decide that Florida humidity isn’t for you and relocate to the crisp air of Colorado.

  

When that happens, the FCC expects you to update your address immediately. Forgetting to do so isn’t just a minor slip-up; it’s a compliance risk.

  

### Updating Your Address: The (Not-So-Hard) Steps

The good news? Updating your address with the FCC is refreshingly straightforward:

  

1.  [Log into the Universal Licensing System (ULS)](https://apps.fcc.gov/cores/userLogin.do)
     with your FCC Registration Number (FRN).
2.  Choose the license you need to update.
3.  Input your shiny new address.
4.  Certify, submit, and pat yourself on the back.

Repeat this anytime your address changes. **If you use a virtual address, the need for updates drops dramatically**—stability and compliance, sorted.

![Smartphone showing a virtual mailbox app with a “QSL Card” notification.](https://bizee.com/_next/image?url=https%3A%2F%2Fs3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com%2Fbizee-website-assets%2Fham-radio-virtual-mailbox-app-ui.webp&w=3840&q=75)

The Bottom Line? Privacy, Compliance, and Staying On-Air
--------------------------------------------------------

  

Ham radio operators are storytellers. Innovators. Connectors of worlds and people. But to keep those call signs crackling, you need to play by the FCC’s rules—and that starts with your address.

  

A [virtual address](https://bizee.com/form/virtual-address-ham-radio)
 might not be the first thing you think of when you fire up your rig, but it just might be the thing that lets you operate with peace of mind. No lost mail. No public exposure. Just you, your radio, and the freedom to connect.

State-by-State Guides to Virtual Address

There are some state-by-state differences for virtual business addresses. In most states, however, the regulatory differences have less to do with the virtual address itself, but rather what business functions the virtual address and digital mail scanning can be used for.

![Arrow Right White Light](https://fls-9e98adad-e144-4ff5-b4ac-e9717504d40a.laravel.cloud/icons/arrow-right-white-light.svg)

  ![Texas Guides To Virtual Address](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvdmlydHVhbC1hZGRyZXNzL3RleGFzLWd1aWRlcy10by12aXJ0dWFsLWFkZHJlc3MucG5n/texas-guides-to-virtual-address.png?p=lg&fm=webp)

![Check Overflow Blue](https://fls-9e98adad-e144-4ff5-b4ac-e9717504d40a.laravel.cloud/icons/check-overflow-blue.svg)

Especially if you live in a state with a reputation for lots of regulatory rules or have heard relevant anecdotes from other business owners in the state, you may want to review our guide to virtual addresses in your state.

Especially if you live in a state with a reputation for lots of regulatory rules or have heard relevant anecdotes from other business owners in the state, you may want to review our guide to virtual addresses in your state.

Frequently Asked Questions


------------------------------

*   1
    
    How do I know when I have new business mail?
    
    You can view your scanned mail online anytime through your secure dashboard. As a default, you'll receive instant email notifications when new mail is available.
    
*   2
    
    What happens after my mail is received?
    
    Once your mail is scanned and uploaded for you to view online, digital copies are securely stored for the entire length of your subscription. After 1-2 weeks, we securely shred the physical copies using enterprise-grade shredders and disposal processes. We protect your trade secrets and your basic privacy while getting rid of the paper clutter.
    
*   3
    
    Does this service include mail forwarding?
    
    Our Business Virtual Address service is not a mail forwarding service. We only forward checks and debit or credit cards to a U.S. address you provide. All other mail is scanned in high-resolution color and securely uploaded to your account for easy online access. We do not accept packages or oversized deliveries and will return these to the sender.
    
*   4
    
    Why do I need to complete USPS Form 1583?
    
    To comply with federal postal regulations, all virtual address users must complete USPS [Form 1583](https://about.usps.com/forms/ps1583.pdf)
    . This form authorizes us to receive mail on your behalf and ensures your mail is handled legally and securely. Without this form, we cannot activate your mailbox. It is a required step for all customers using a Commercial Mail Receiving Agency like ours.  
      
    
    You need two forms of identification: At least one must be a government-issued photo ID, such as a driver’s license or passport. The second can be a non-photo ID that verifies your name and address. Common examples include a lease agreement or mortgage, home or car insurance policy, voter card, or vehicle registration. All documents must be valid and unexpired.
    
*   5
    
    Does the IRS accept virtual addresses?
    
    Yes, for the most part. Most businesses experience zero trouble using their virtual business address for things like applying for an EIN and filing business taxes. In fact, corresponding with the IRS is one of the big differences between a P.O. Box and a virtual address solution. The IRS does not allow businesses to use P.O. Boxes for official correspondence. Another exception to the rule: You cannot use a virtual address (personal or business) to file your personal tax returns.
    
*   6
    
    Will banks accept a virtual address?
    
    Yes, in most cases. Much like the IRS, many banks will readily accept a virtual address for a business banking account, while requiring a home address for personal banking. Some local brick-and-mortar banks may have reservations if you’re using a virtual address for a high-risk business, but this is rare.
    
*   7
    
    What is the difference between a virtual business address, a virtual mailbox, and a virtual business office?
    
    A virtual business address is the street address and physical location where the mail is sent for handling and processing. A virtual mailbox is the secure dashboard and digital mail scans that allows customers to view, organize, and upload their mail. A virtual business office is a software platform that allows you to communicate, conduct meetings, manage workflows, and leverage digital team-building exercises. Virtual offices do not typically include a virtual address with their services.
    
*   8
    
    Can I use my virtual address as a registered agent?
    
    No, these are two distinct services. You can't use a virtual address service to [comply with registered agent requirements](https://bizee.com/business-management/registered-agent)
    .
    
*   9
    
    Can I get a virtual address for personal use?
    
    Yes, the big difference is that a personal virtual address must use your legal name, not the name of your business. Per state rules, these addresses must be strictly for personal use. Sole proprietors doing business in their own name CAN use this type of address.

# Business Entity Comparison: Choose the Right Structure for You

Business Entity Comparison: Choose the Right Structure for You

Different Types of Corporate Structures

Limited Liability Company (LLC)

LLC Limited Liability Protection

Types of Tax an LLC is Liable For

#### Different Types of Corporate Structures

#### You’ll learn about the four main types of business entity below — LLCs, S Corporations, C Corporations and nonprofits, so you can decide which will best meet your needs.

#### Limited Liability Company (LLC)

#### The LLC is one of the most popular types of business entities. It’s ideally suited for smaller organizations and startups, for several reasons:

*   LLCs are fast and easy to setup.  
      
    
*   LLCs have a simple business structure.  
      
    
*   Forming an LLC is generally inexpensive.  
      
    
*   Running an LLC is easier than running a C Corp or S Corp.  
      
    
*   There are fewer rules, regulations and legal compliance issues for LLCs.  
      
    
*   LLCs are formed and regulated on a state level.

#### The cost and policies governing an LLC do vary from state to state. Check out our [LLC State Information](https://bizee.com/llc-state-information)
 resource for additional info on your state.

#### LLC Limited Liability Protection

#### Like C Corps and S Corps, LLCs provide their owners with limited liability protection. This means the business assets are owned separately by the LLC, not by the owners. Any liability the business has (e.g. monies owed, equipment, depreciation, lawsuits, etc.) are purely the liability of the business, and do not (generally) have any impact on the individual owner’s personal assets.

#### Types of Tax an LLC is Liable For

#### It’s important to note that an LLC will be liable for certain types of tax, for example:

*   Payroll tax on salaries paid to employees (but not to members or owners — they will pay self-employment tax on their personal tax returns).  
      
    
*   Sales tax on goods purchased by and for the business.  
      
    
*   Property taxes on owned business property.  
      
    
*   In certain cases, other types of tax or tariffs may need to be paid by an LLC.  
      
    
*   Generally, these taxes can be subtracted as business expenses and do not flow through to individual owner’s tax returns.

Protection

Limited Liability Protection

**LLC**

LLCs provide personal asset protection, which shields you from being personally liable for business debts.

**C-Corp**

C Corps provide personal asset protection, which shields you from being personally liable for business debts.

**S-Corp**

S Corps provide personal asset protection, which shields you from being personally liable for business debts.

**Nonprofit**

Nonprofits provide personal asset protection, which shields you from being personally liable for business debts.

**Nonprofit**

Nonprofits provide personal asset protection, which shields you from being personally liable for business debts.

State Filing Fees

State Formation Fees

**LLC**

LLCs are required to pay formation fees to the state. Fees will vary based on the state of incorporation.

**C-Corp**

C Corps are required to pay formation fees to the state. Fees will vary based on the state of incorporation.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are required to pay formation fees to the state. Fees will vary based on the state of incorporation.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits are required to pay formation fees to the state. Fees will vary based on the state of incorporation.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits are required to pay formation fees to the state. Fees will vary based on the state of incorporation.

Ongoing Compliance Fees

**LLC**

Depending on the state of incorporation, reports and fees may be required.

**C-Corp**

An annual report and franchise fees are generally due each year along with other reports and fees, which varies depending on the state of incorporation.

**S-Corp**

An annual report and franchise fees are generally due each year along with other reports and fees, which varies depending on the state of incorporation.

**Non-Profit**

For Nonprofits this varies from state to state.

**Non-Profit**

Managing Your Business Fees

Flexible Management Structure

**LLC**

LLCs must be member or manager managed according to the terms of the operating agreement.

**C-Corp**

C Corps are required to have shareholder elected directors who oversee and elect officers to run the day-to-day operations of the company.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are required to have shareholder elected directors who oversee and elect officers to run the day-to-day operations of the company.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits are managed by their board of directors following the regulations set forth in their Bylaws.

**LLC**

LLCs must be member or manager managed according to the terms of the operating agreement.

**C-Corp**

C Corps are required to have shareholder elected directors who oversee and elect officers to run the day-to-day operations of the company.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are required to have shareholder elected directors who oversee and elect officers to run the day-to-day operations of the company.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits are managed by their board of directors following the regulations set forth in their Bylaws.

Adding/Transferring Ownership

**LLC**

Changes in ownership of an LLC are dependent on the terms of the operating agreement.

**C-Corp**

Ownership changes in a C Corp are easily made through the sell of stock to new or existing shareholders.

**S-Corp**

Ownership changes in an S Corp are easily made through the sell of stock to new or existing shareholders.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits have no owners.

**LLC**

Changes in ownership of an LLC are dependent on the terms of the operating agreement.

**C-Corp**

Ownership changes in a C Corp are easily made through the sell of stock to new or existing shareholders.

**S-Corp**

Ownership changes in an S Corp are easily made through the sell of stock to new or existing shareholders.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits have no owners.

Ongoing Requirements

**LLC**

Depending on the state of incorporation, an LLC may be required to file an annual report and/or pay franchise fees.

**C-Corp**

After formation, C Corps have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, holding initial and annual shareholder meetings, and issuing stock.

**S-Corp**

After formation, S Corps have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, holding initial and annual shareholder meetings, and issuing stock.

**Non-Profit**

After formation, Nonprofits have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, and seeking tax exempt status.

**LLC**

Depending on the state of incorporation, an LLC may be required to file an annual report and/or pay franchise fees.

**C-Corp**

After formation, C Corps have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, holding initial and annual shareholder meetings, and issuing stock.

**S-Corp**

After formation, S Corps have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, holding initial and annual shareholder meetings, and issuing stock.

**Non-Profit**

After formation, Nonprofits have many ongoing formalities such as writing bylaws, selecting directors, and seeking tax exempt status.

Ease of Raising Capital

**LLC**

LLCs are not allowed to sell stock but may be able to raise capital via bank loans and various other avenues.

**C-Corp**

C Corps may issue many types of stocks, which may be sold to an unlimited number of shareholders.

**S-Corp**

S Corps may issue one type of stock, which may be sold to a maximum of 100 shareholders.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits may obtain bank loans, grants, venture capital, and tax-exempt donations. In some states, Nonprofits may sell stock.

**LLC**

LLCs are not allowed to sell stock but may be able to raise capital via bank loans and various other avenues.

**C-Corp**

C Corps may issue many types of stocks, which may be sold to an unlimited number of shareholders.

**S-Corp**

S Corps may issue one type of stock, which may be sold to a maximum of 100 shareholders.

**Non-Profit**

Nonprofits may obtain bank loans, grants, venture capital, and tax-exempt donations. In some states, Nonprofits may sell stock.

Tax

Pass-through Taxation

**LLC**

LLCs are not taxed at the corporate level. Instead, all profit and losses are reported with the personal income taxes of each member.

**C-Corp**

The income of the C Corp is taxed at the corporate level and then again at the shareholder level.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not taxed at the corporate level. Instead, all profit and losses are reported with the personal income taxes of each shareholder (owner).

**Non-Profit**

The income of Nonprofits is taxed at the corporate level unless they apply for and are granted tax-exempt status.

**LLC**

LLCs are not taxed at the corporate level. Instead, all profit and losses are reported with the personal income taxes of each member.

**C-Corp**

The income of the C Corp is taxed at the corporate level and then again at the shareholder level.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not taxed at the corporate level. Instead, all profit and losses are reported with the personal income taxes of each shareholder (owner).

**Non-Profit**

The income of Nonprofits is taxed at the corporate level unless they apply for and are granted tax-exempt status.

Double Taxation

**LLC**

LLCs are not taxed at the corporate level.

**C-Corp**

The income of the C Corp is taxed at the corporate level and then again at the shareholder level.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not taxed at the corporate level.

**Non-Profit**

The income of Nonprofits is taxed at the corporate level unless they apply for and are granted tax-exempt status.

**LLC**

LLCs are not taxed at the corporate level.

**C-Corp**

The income of the C Corp is taxed at the corporate level and then again at the shareholder level.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not taxed at the corporate level.

**Non-Profit**

The income of Nonprofits is taxed at the corporate level unless they apply for and are granted tax-exempt status.

Tax Exempt

**LLC**

LLCs are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

**C-Corp**

C Corps are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

**Non-Profit**

The income of Nonprofits is taxed at the corporate level unless they apply for and are granted tax-exempt status.

**LLC**

LLCs are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

**C-Corp**

C Corps are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

**S-Corp**

S Corps are not eligible for tax-exempt status.

Forming a C Corporation Can Be Time Consuming and Expensive

C Corporation registration is complex. Multiple bodies, including the federal government, require to meet different conditions. There are also state-specific rules and regulations you must adhere to. Formation is a multistep process & filing errors could result in costly and serious consequences.

Common Questions About Starting a C Corporation


---------------------------------------------------

*   1
    
    Can I Start a C Corporation For Free?
    
    Yes! With our $0 C Corporation formation package, you only pay the fees required by your state. Bizee’s filing services are free.
    
*   2
    
    How Much Does Your Service Cost?
    
    Since 2004 we’ve been honing & perfecting our service. Our tech-enabled process efficiencies mean that we can keep the costs down and pass this incredible value on to you. The result is low-cost yet personalized business formation with friendly and fast service.
    
    The Basic Package costs $0 + state fee and includes the basics needed to start a C Corporation.
    
    The Standard Package is $149 + state fee. It’s the option most clients choose and boasts a comprehensive feature set to get your business started. Your EIN Business Tax number is included (whilst most other incorporation services charge an extra fee on top of their equivalent package price for this). The Standard package also includes IRS Form 2553, Corporation Bylaws, Operating Agreement, Banking Resolution, Lifetime Company Alerts, Online Access Dashboard, Unlimited Phone and Email Support, Business Banking Account & Business Tax Consultation.
    
    The Premium Package is our best value package at $299 + state fee and it offers a full suite of features. Premium includes all of the Standard benefits plus Business Contract Templates, Expedited Filing and Domain Name plus Business Email.
    
    When you form your Nonprofit with us, our Registered Agent service is free for the first year and is only $119 per year after that.
    
    For more information on our services and prices, visit our [how it works](https://bizee.com/how-it-works)
     page.
    
*   3
    
    Are There Specific Rules For My State?
    
    Each state has specific rules and requirements regarding Registered Agents, naming rules, business licenses etc. Learn more about C Corporations in your state and read our free C Corporation state guides [here](https://bizee.com/corp-formation-by-state)
    .
    
*   4
    
    What's My State's Filing Fee for C Corporations?
    
    Filing costs to form a C Corporation can vary from state to state. Use [our free filing fees](https://bizee.com/state-filing-fees)
     chart to easily compare state fees before you start your business.
    
*   5
    
    Are There Any Hidden Costs?
    
    No! We pride ourselves on transparency. There are absolutely no hidden costs associated with forming your business.
    
    With our $0 C Corporation package, you only pay the fee required by your state. This is the state fee for forming a C Corp that you’d need to pay even if you were doing the entire process on your own. Some states charge online processing fees to file your paperwork, but those fees come from the state, not from Bizee. Bizee’s services are entirely free if you choose the $0 C Corporation package.
    
    Our mission is to provide you with a modern and superior experience with unparalleled value. Think of us as your business guide. We make registering a C Corporation as easy and low cost as possible, so you can focus on the important things.
    
*   6
    
    How Long Does it Take to File a C Corporation Online?
    
    Bizee’s standard processing time to send your data onto the relevant state is 1 day.
    
    State filing times vary from three to twelve weeks. You have the option to pay an expedited fee for Bizee to process your paperwork faster (included in Premium package). Sometimes your chosen state may also offer expedited processing through their systems too - if this is the case, we’ll let you know it’s an option. Easily compare state filing times here.
    
*   7
    
    Do You Have Any Guides or Resources For Getting Started?
    
    Yes, we have a lot of helpful content! Learn more about C Corporations [here](https://bizee.com/what-is-c-corporation)
    . Check out our [Resource Center](https://bizee.com/blog/tag/form-a-business)
     for in depth information on every aspect of planning, starting and growing your business.
    
*   8
    
    Do You Provide Hands-On Support?
    
    Of course! We believe in educating our customers and providing a wide variety of guidance at every step in the formation process and beyond.
    
    If you require additional support, you can contact us via Help Chat in your personalized dashboard. We do also offer customer service to assist with any transactional questions.
    
    Prefer to speak to an incorporation specialist over the phone? Get in touch on 844-830-8267 Monday – Friday from 9 a.m. to 6 p.m. CST.
    

  ![Man Carving Wood Desktop](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvcmFuZG9tLWN0YS1iYW5uZXJzL21hbi1jYXJ2aW5nLXdvb2QtZGVza3RvcC53ZWJw/man-carving-wood-desktop.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)

Also included in the Gold package are IRS Form 2553, Corporation Bylaws, Operating Agreement, Banking Resolution, Lifetime Company Alerts, Online Access Dashboard, Unlimited Phone & Email Support, Business Banking Account, and Business Tax Consultation.  
      
    The Premium Package is $299 + state fee. It’s our best value package offering a full suite of features. It includes all of the Gold benefits plus Business Contract Templates, Expedited Filing, and Domain Name + Business Email.  
      
    When you form your Nonprofit with us, our Registered Agent service is free for the first year and is only $119 per year after that.  
      
    For more information on our services and prices, [visit our how it works page](https://bizee.com/how-it-works)
    .
    
*   3
    
    Which Type of Nonprofit Organization is Right for Me?
    
    There are four main types of Nonprofit in the United States. Each has subtly different goals and corporate structure, but all are tax-exempt!  
      
    **Public Charities/501(c)(3) Organizations**  
    Charities, also known as 501(c)(3) organizations, usually provide low-cost or free services to the public utilizing funds received through donations. This can be via private donations or fundraising events specifically designed to secure funding from members or advocates. Examples of public charities include food banks and animal welfare organizations.  
      
    **Social Advocacy Organizations**  
    This type of Nonprofit is member-based and aims to achieve specific goals regarding political change without achieving a profit. Social advocacy organizations, classified by the IRS as 501(c)(4), use donations and member dues to send out information that promotes a particular social agenda. The NAACP and the ACLU are social advocacy organizations you might be familiar with.  
      
    **Foundations**  
    Like charities, foundations are also classified as 501(c)(3) organizations. They work to better the community, whether contributing financially to local, smaller charities/nonprofits or holding events that benefit communities. Foundations are funded by and contribute on behalf of an associated for-profit corporation. Foundations must donate a certain amount of income to other organizations every year. The Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation is one of the most well-known.  
      
    **Trade and Professional Organizations**  
    These types of organizations are classified as 501(c)(6). They usually work to benefit and promote members’ business interests and are funded primarily through membership dues. Common trade and professional organizations include chambers of commerce and real estate boards.
    
*   4
    
    Are There Specific Rules For My State?
    
    Each state has specific rules for registration, registered agents, annual reporting, and other requirements. Bizee will help you determine what you need to be compliant in your specific state as part of the Nonprofit formation process.

Table of Contents

Here's What Can and Cannot Be Trademarked

What Is a Trademark?

What Can Be Trademarked?

What Things Can You Not Trademark?

Should You File a Trademark?

Ready to Protect Your Biz with a Trademark?

Here's What Can and Cannot Be Trademarked

There comes a point in every entrepreneur's journey when they start thinking about trademarks. Maybe it happens when they commission their first custom logo, or maybe it's when they switch from a slogan they're not crazy about to one they love.  
  
If you've reached that point in your small business adventure, then it's time to learn what can be trademarked so you can better protect your company's intellectual properties from infringement.

What Is a Trademark?

If you run your own business, then you've probably heard of trademarks before, and you may have even contemplated [filing one yourself](https://bizee.com/articles/file-trademark-on-your-own)
.  
  
After all, trademarks are nothing if not popular — between Q4 2019 and Q2 2022, the number of active trademark registrations swelled from just under 2.5 million to nearly 3 million ([Source](https://www.uspto.gov/dashboard/trademarks/)
).  
  
But before we start clearing up what can and cannot be trademarked, let's first define what a trademark actually is.  
  
According to the [U.S. Patent and Trademark Office (USPTO)](https://www.uspto.gov/trademarks/basics/what-trademark)
: A trademark can be any word, phrase, symbol, design, or a combination of these things that identifies your goods or services. It’s how customers recognize you in the marketplace and distinguish you from your competitors.  
  
To complicate things slightly, a trademark can refer to both a trademark and a service mark. A service mark is similar to a trademark except that it applies to services instead of goods.  
  
So what's the point of a trademark? As per the USPTO, a trademark can help to:  
  

*   Identify the brand behind your products or services
*   Provide legal protection for your brand
*   Prevent counterfeiting and fraud

  
Knowing this, it's easy to see why so many trademarks are filed — they can be immensely valuable to businesses looking to protect their brand from copycats and fraudsters.

   ![Whats A Trademark Toc](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvd2hhdHMtYS10cmFkZW1hcmstdG9jLndlYnA/whats-a-trademark-toc.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)  ![Whats A Trademark Toc Mobile](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvd2hhdHMtYS10cmFkZW1hcmstdG9jLW1vYmlsZS53ZWJw/whats-a-trademark-toc-mobile.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)

A trademark can be any word, phrase, symbol, design, or a combination of these things that identifies your goods or services. It’s how customers recognize you in the marketplace and distinguish you from your competitors.

What Can Be Trademarked?

Given the benefits that trademarks provide, it would be understandable if businesses trademarked everything they created. But unfortunately, trademarks can only be used to protect certain things, and they must be unique.

  
Here are the properties that can be trademarked, along with a few real-life examples:  
  

*   **Brand names**
    *   Apple, Microsoft and Ford  
          
        
*   **Phrases/slogans**
    *   McDonald's "I'm lovin' it," Capital One's "What's in your wallet?" and Skittles' "Taste the rainbow"  
          
        
*   **Product names**
    *   Kawasaki's "Jet Ski," Pfizer's "Listerine" and 7-Eleven's "Slurpee"  
          
        
*   **Symbols/logos**
    *   Nike's swoosh, Chanel's double C monogram and NBC's peacock  
          
        
*   **Colors**
    *   Tiffany & Co's signature shade of blue, John Deere's combination of green and yellow and Post-it's yellow hue  
          
        
*   **Shapes**
    *   Toblerone's triangular chocolate bars, Hershey's conical Kisses and Weber's kettle-shaped grills  
          
        
*   **Sounds**
    *   the roar of MGM's lion, NBC's chimes and Nokia's classic ringtones  
          
        
*   **Fictional characters**
    *   Disney's Mickey Mouse, Planters' Mr. Peanut and Marvel's Captain America  
          
        
*   **Combinations thereof**, such as the color and design of Starbucks' green mermaid logo, Google's distinctively multi-colored logo and 20th Century Fox's orchestral fanfare playing behind its logo

  
As you can see, trademarks can be applied to many aspects of a company's branding.  
  
If you're interested in using trademarks to protect your small business, it's often wise to start by filing them for properties you know can be covered, such as your company's unique name, logo and slogan.  
  
Just remember to conduct a thorough [trademark search](https://bizee.com/business-formation/trademark-registration#)
 first to ensure that your desired trademark (or one very similar to it) hasn't already been filed by someone else.

What Things Can You Not Trademark?

There's a limit to what can be protected by trademark, and some people learn this the hard way when their trademark filing is [rejected by the USPTO](https://www.uspto.gov/trademarks/additional-guidance-and-resources/possible-grounds-refusal-mark)
.  
  
To avoid becoming one of those people and making [costly trademark mistakes](https://bizee.com/articles/trademark-business-name)
, be sure to familiarize yourself with the properties that cannot be trademarked. Here they are, along with examples:  
  

*   **Generic words and phrases**
    *   "genuine," "craft store" or "made in USA"  
          
        
*   **Merely descriptive words and phrases**
    *   "delicious" or "world's most delicious muffins"  
          
        
*   **Deceptively descriptive words and phrases**
    *   "real beef dog food" for dog food that doesn't actually contain real beef  
          
        
*   **Primarily geographically descriptive words and phrases**
    *   "Maine lobster," "Florida oranges" or "New York Pizza"  
          
        
*   **Primarily geographically deceptively descriptive words and phrases**
    *   "Wisconsin Signature Creamery" for dairy products not produced in Wisconsin  
          
        
*   **Merely a surname**
    *   "Brown's Automotive" or "Smith Antiques"  
          
        
*   **Ornamentation**
    *   "live, laugh, love" printed on a pillow  
          
        
*   **Similarity to an existing trademark**
    *   Trying to trademark a phrase that could be easily confused with that of another company in the same field

  
So what phrases cannot be trademarked? The answer is any phrase that is generic, merely descriptive, deceptive, based only on a surname or place, purely ornamental or similar to another trademark.

What If You Want to Use Someone's Trademark?

While we're on the topic of things you can't trademark, let's talk about what to do if you want to use someone's trademark. For instance, you may want to sell merchandise that features a trademarked character (e.g., Elmo) or logo (e.g., Coca-Cola's).

  
Or, you may want to demonstrate how your brand performs in comparison to a competitor with a trademarked name (e.g., your household cleaner vs. Lysol).

  
In cases such as those, you can generally choose between two options:  
  
  
**1\. Ask for permission**, sign a licensing agreement and pay any requisite licensing fees.  
**2\. Use the property under the [fair use doctrine](https://www.copyright.gov/fair-use/more-info.html)
**, such as for criticism, commentary or educational purposes.

  
Whatever route you take, just be sure that you're within your legal limits beforehand. If you don't, you might find yourself in hot water and possibly even liable for [trademark infringement](https://www.uspto.gov/page/about-trademark-infringement)
 damages.

   ![What If You Want Toc](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvd2hhdC1pZi15b3Utd2FudC10b2Mud2VicA/what-if-you-want-toc.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)  ![What If You Want Toc Mobile](https://bizee.com/img/http/aHR0cHM6Ly9mbHMtOWU5OGFkYWQtZTE0NC00ZmY1LWI0YWMtZTk3MTc1MDRkNDBhLmxhcmF2ZWwuY2xvdWQvd2hhdC1pZi15b3Utd2FudC10b2MtbW9iaWxlLndlYnA/what-if-you-want-toc-mobile.webp?p=lg&fm=webp)

Knowing this, it's easy to see why so many trademarks are filed — they can be immensely valuable to businesses looking to protect their brand from copycats and fraudsters.

Should You File a Trademark?

So when should you start filling out a trademark application to protect your business's intellectual properties? That all depends on the potential strength of your trademark.  
  
As the USPTO explains, [the strongest trademarks](https://www.uspto.gov/trademarks/basics/strong-trademarks)
 are fanciful (e.g., "Kodak" to describe a camera company) or arbitrary (e.g., "Galaxy" to describe a smartphone). On the other hand, the weakest trademarks are generic names that aren't unique to any company or product.  
  
If the property you're considering trademarking falls on the strong side of the spectrum, then a trademark may be just what you need to protect the brand you've worked so hard to create.  
  
But what if the property you want to trademark falls on the weak side of the spectrum? No worries — as long as you change it to be stronger, you can still get a trademark.  
  
For instance, if you have a business named "Texas BBQ," it will be considered primarily geographically descriptive and thus won't be eligible for a trademark.  
  
So, you can simply add a word or two to make it unique and trademark-worthy — "Lilian's Texas BBQ" or "Pecan & Prairie BBQ" might be acceptable alternatives.

Ready to Protect Your Biz with a Trademark?

When you're ready to apply for a trademark, we can help you streamline the process. With Bizee's trademark registration service, we'll assist you with research, legal guidance and paperwork filing so you can rest easy knowing no detail's been overlooked.
